Each of those subscriptions is viewed as a \"watch\" on X, while behind the scenes\n49: // there is just a single real subscription to that resource name.\n50: //\n51: // This class maintains the watches<-->subscription mapping: it\n52: // 1) delivers updates to all interested watches, and\n53: // 2) tracks which resource names should be {added to,removed from} the subscription when the\n54: //    {first,last} watch on a resource name is {added,removed}.\n55: //\n56: // #1 is accomplished by WatchMap's implementation of the SubscriptionCallbacks interface.\n57: // This interface allows the xDS client to just throw each xDS update message it receives directly\n58: // into WatchMap::onConfigUpdate, rather than having to track the various watches' callbacks.\n59: //\n60: // The information for #2 is returned by updateWatchInterest(); the caller should use it to\n61: // update the subscription accordingly.\n62: //\n63: // A WatchMap is assumed to be dedicated to a single type_url type of resource (EDS, CDS, etc).\n64: //\n65: // The WatchMap can also store the fetched resources in a cache, and allow others to fetch\n66: // resources directly from the cache. This is done for EDS in the following case:\n67: // Assume an active EDS cluster exists with some load-assignment that is kept in the cache.\n68: // If the cluster is updated, and no load-assignment is sent from the xDS server, the\n69: // cached version will be used.\n70: // The WatchMap is responsible to update the cache with the resource contents, and it is\n71: // up to the specific xDS type subscription handler (i.e., EdsClusterImpl), to fetch\n72: // the resource from the cache.\n73: class WatchMap : public UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks, public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\n74: public:\n75:   WatchMap(const bool use_namespace_matching, const std::string& type_url,\n76:            CustomConfigValidators* config_validators, EdsResourcesCacheOptRef eds_resources_cache)\n77:       : use_namespace_matching_(use_namespace_matching), type_url_(type_url),\n78:         config_validators_(config_validators), eds_resources_cache_(eds_resources_cache) {\n79:     // If eds resources cache is provided, then the type must be ClusterLoadAssignment.\n80:     ASSERT(!eds_resources_cache_.has_value() ||\n81:            (type_url == Config::getTypeUrl<envoy::config::endpoint::v3::ClusterLoadAssignment>()));\n82:   }\n83: \n84:   // Adds 'callbacks' to the WatchMap, with every possible resource being watched.\n85:   // (Use updateWatchInterest() to narrow it down to some specific names).\n86:   // Returns the newly added watch, to be used with updateWatchInterest and removeWatch.\n87:   Watch* addWatch(SubscriptionCallbacks& callbacks, OpaqueResourceDecoder& resource_decoder);\n88: \n89:   // Updates the set of resource names that the given watch should watch.\n90:   // Returns any resource name additions/removals that are unique across all watches. That is:\n91:   // 1) if 'resources' contains X and no other watch cares about X, X will be in added_.\n92:   // 2) if 'resources' does not contain Y, and this watch was the only one that cared about Y,\n93:   //    Y will be in removed_.\n94:   AddedRemoved updateWatchInterest(Watch* watch,\n95:                                    const absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>& update_to_these_names);\n96: \n97:   // Expects that the watch to be removed has already had all of its resource names removed via\n98:   // updateWatchInterest().\n99:   void removeWatch(Watch* watch);\n100: \n101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/envoyproxy/envoy@99ddbc21deba65d2288107e67e693550ac7091f3/-/blob/source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/watch_map.h%3FL1-100"}}}

Note that the implementation is currently considered \"\n78:                       \"experimental and may be modified in future Envoy versions!\");\n79:       // Only create the retry timer if failover is supported.\n80:       complete_retry_timer_ = dispatcher.createTimer([this]() -> void { retryConnections(); });\n81:       failover_callbacks_ = std::make_unique<FailoverGrpcStreamCallbacks>(*this);\n82:       GrpcStreamCreator& failover_stream_creator_ref = failover_stream_creator.value();\n83:       failover_grpc_stream_ = std::move(failover_stream_creator_ref(failover_callbacks_.get()));\n84:       ASSERT(failover_grpc_stream_ != nullptr);\n85:     }\n86:   }\n87: \n88:   virtual ~GrpcMuxFailover() = default;\n89: \n90:   // Attempts to establish a new stream to the either the primary or failover source.\n91:   void establishNewStream() override {\n92:     // Attempt establishing a connection to the primary source.\n93:     // This method may be called multiple times, even if the primary/failover stream\n94:     // is already established or in the process of being established.\n95:     if (complete_retry_timer_) {\n96:       complete_retry_timer_->disableTimer();\n97:     }\n98:     // If already connected to one of the source, return.\n99:     if (connection_state_ == ConnectionState::ConnectedToPrimary ||\n100:         connection_state_ == ConnectionState::ConnectedToFailover) {\n101:       ENVOY_LOG_MISC(trace,\n102:                      \"Already connected to an xDS server, skipping establishNewStream() call\");\n103:       return;\n104:     }\n105:     if (!Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\n106:             \"envoy.reloadable_features.xds_failover_to_primary_enabled\")) {\n107:       // Allow stickiness, so if Envoy was ever connected to the primary source only\n108:       // retry to reconnect to the primary source, If Envoy was ever connected to the\n109:       // failover source then only retry to reconnect to the failover source.\n110:       if (previously_connected_to_ == ConnectedTo::Primary) {\n111:         ENVOY_LOG_MISC(\n112:             info, \"Previously connected to the primary xDS source, attempting to reconnect to it\");\n113:         connection_state_ = ConnectionState::ConnectingToFailover;\n120:         failover_grpc_stream_->establishNewStream();\n121:         return;\n122:       }\n123:     }\n124:     // connection_state_ is either None, ConnectingToPrimary or\n125:     // ConnectingToFailover. In the first 2 cases try to connect to the primary\n126:     // (preferring the primary in the case of None), and in the third case\n127:     // try to connect to the failover.\n128:     // Note that if a connection to the primary source was ever successful, the\n129:     // failover manager will keep setting connection_state_ to either None or\n130:     // ConnectingToPrimary, which ensures that only the primary stream will be\n131:     // established.\n132:     if (connection_state_ == ConnectionState::ConnectingToFailover) {\n133:       ASSERT(!ever_connected_to_primary_);\n134:       failover_grpc_stream_->establishNewStream();\n135:     } else {\n136:       ASSERT(connection_state_ == ConnectionState::None ||\n137:              connection_state_ == ConnectionState::ConnectingToPrimary);\n138:       connection_state_ = ConnectionState::ConnectingToPrimary;\n139:       primary_grpc_stream_->establishNewStream();\n140:     }\n141:   }\n142: \n143:   // Returns the availability of the underlying stream.\n144:   bool grpcStreamAvailable() const override {\n145:     if (connectingToOrConnectedToFailover()) {\n146:       return failover_grpc_stream_->grpcStreamAvailable();\n147:     }\n148:     // Either connecting/connected to the primary, or no connection was attempted.\n149:     return primary_grpc_stream_->grpcStreamAvailable();\n150:   }\n151: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/envoyproxy/envoy@99ddbc21deba65d2288107e67e693550ac7091f3/-/blob/source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_failover.h%3FL1-150"}}}

(The push() doesn't matter\n129:     // because we always attempt this drain immediately after the push). Basically, a change in\n130:     // queue length is not \"meaningful\" until it has persisted until here. We need the\n131:     // if(>0 || used) to keep this stat from being wrongly marked interesting by a pointless set(0)\n132:     // and needlessly taking up space. The first time we set(123), used becomes true, and so we will\n133:     // subsequently always do the set (including set(0)).\n134:     if (size > 0 || control_plane_stats_.pending_requests_.used()) {\n135:       control_plane_stats_.pending_requests_.set(size);\n136:     }\n137:   }\n138: \n139:   bool checkRateLimitAllowsDrain() override {\n140:     if (!rate_limiting_enabled_ || limit_request_->consume(1, false)) {\n141:       return true;\n142:     }\n143:     ASSERT(drain_request_timer_ != nullptr);\n144:     control_plane_stats_.rate_limit_enforced_.inc();\n145:     // Enable the drain request timer.\n146:     if (!drain_request_timer_->enabled()) {\n147:       drain_request_timer_->enableTimer(limit_request_->nextTokenAvailable());\n148:     }\n149:     return false;\n150:   }\n151: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/envoyproxy/envoy@99ddbc21deba65d2288107e67e693550ac7091f3/-/blob/source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_stream.h%3FL1-150"}}}

implementation is located in the source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc directory of the envoyproxy/envoy repository. The implementation consists of several key components:\\n\\n## Core gRPC Mux Implementation (xds_mux namespace)\\n\\nThe newest and most modular implementation is in the xds_mux subdirectory (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/). This includes:\\n\\n1. **GrpcMuxImpl (grpc_mux_impl.h/cc)** - A templated base class that manages subscriptions to one or more resource types. It implements two concrete variants:\\n   - GrpcMuxDelta: Implements Delta xDS protocol (incremental updates)\\n   - GrpcMuxSotw: Implements State-of-the-World xDS protocol (full resource snapshots)\\n   Both handle multiplexing multiple resource types (EDS, CDS, LDS, RDS) over a single gRPC stream.\\n\\n2. **Delta xDS State Machine (delta_subscription_state.h/cc)** - Tracks the protocol state of delta xDS sessions for individual resource types. Manages:\\n   - Requested resource tracking with per-resource versions\\n   - Wildcard vs specific resource subscriptions\\n   - Resource TTL (time-to-live) for heartbeat support\\n   - Subscription interest changes\\n\\n3. **SotW xDS State Machine (sotw_subscription_state.h/cc)** - Tracks state-of-the-world xDS sessions, managing version information and resource updates.\\n\\n4. **Subscription State Base Class (subscription_state.h)** - Provides the abstract BaseSubscriptionState template that both delta and SotW implementations inherit from. Handles:\\n   - ACK/NACK generation via getNextRequestWithAck()\\n   - Response handling through handleResponse()\\n   - Error detail formatting for rejections\\n\\n## gRPC Stream Handler\\n\\n**GrpcStream (grpc_stream.h)** - Manages the bidirectional gRPC stream to the xDS server. It:\\n- Establishes and maintains the connection\\n- Receives discovery responses via onReceiveMessage()\\n- Sends discovery requests\\n- Handles rate limiting and backoff strategy\\n- Implements Grpc::AsyncStreamCallbacks interface\\n\\n## Resource Subscription Tracking\\n\\n**WatchMap (watch_map.h/cc)** - Tracks subscriptions to xDS resources:\\n- Manages \\\"watches\\\" from different Envoy components (e.g., listeners, clusters) for the same resource\\n- Tracks which resource names are currently of interest\\n- Delivers updates to all interested watches\\n- Manages EDS resources cache for endpoint discovery\\n\\n## ACK/NACK Processing\\n\\n**PausableAckQueue (pausable_ack_queue.h/cc)** - Manages the queue of ACK/NACK messages:\\n- Maintains ordering of acknowledgments while respecting pause/resume semantics\\n- Allows pausing ACKs for specific resource types during config processing\\n- Supports head-of-line blocking mitigation\\n\\n**UpdateAck (update_ack.h)** -
